                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Permanente Physicians Retirement Plan Supplement to the
Kaiser Permanente Retirement Plan

Colorado Permanente Medical Group (CPMG) provides eligible employees with the Permanente Physicians
Retirement Plan (PPRP). PPRP is a qualified defined benefit plan. You earn retirement income under this plan
based on a pension formula described in more detail below.

Who Is Eligible

You are eligible to participate in PPRP if you are classified by CPMG as a shareholder Physician, Executive, or
Podiatrist who was hired before July 1, 2016.
Please note: If you were hired after July 1, 2016, you are not eligible to participate in this plan. Instead, you are
eligible to participate in the Cash Balance Plan. In addition, you are not eligible to participate if you are classified
by CPMG as an independent contractor or leased employee, or if you are a physician hired after January 1, 2013,
who is classified as a non-shareholder.

When Your Participation Begins

If you meet the eligibility requirements above, you will automatically become a participant in the plan on the first
day you are employed by CPMG in an eligible classification, regardless of your employment status or work
schedule.

Participation Upon Your Rehire

If you terminate employment and had previously participated in the plan prior to July 1, 2016, you become a
participant in the plan again on your date of rehire as an eligible Physician, Executive, or Podiatrist of CPMG. If
you were not a participant in the plan prior to July 1, 2016, you are not eligible to participate in the plan upon
your rehire. Instead, you are eligible to participate in the CPMG Cash Balance Plan.

Hour of Service

An Hour of Service is any hour, including sick leave, vacation, holidays, and paid leaves of absence, for which you
are compensated as an employee of CPMG or any other Kaiser Permanente entity.

Vesting in Your Benefit

Vesting refers to your entitlement to a benefit. You are 100 percent vested in your benefit under the plan if you are
a participant and meet either of the following conditions: (1) you have at least five Years of Service (see " Year of
Service" ), or (2) you are age 65 or older and are still actively employed by CPMG. If you are vested, you are
entitled to a benefit that will be payable when you turn age 65, or earlier if you meet the age and Years of Service
requirements for early retirement before you terminate employment with CPMG. If you terminate employment
with CPMG without meeting either condition (1) or (2) above, you are not vested and not eligible for a benefit
from the plan.

Year of Service

A Year of Service is any calendar year, whole or part, in which you are compensated for 1,000 or more Hours of
Service. Generally, your compensated hours and certain periods of unpaid leaves count toward this requirement, as
described in more detail in "Years of Service and Credited Service for Leaves."

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 69
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

If you have fewer than 1,000 hours of employment during a calendar year, you will be credited with a fractional
Year of Service for the calendar year equal to your Hours of Service during which you were scheduled to work at
least 20 hours per week divided by 1,000. If you are credited with fewer than 1,000 hours of employment during
any calendar year and not scheduled to work at least 20 hours for any week during such year, you will not be
credited with a full or fractional Year of Service for that calendar year.
Your Years of Service are used for purposes of determining participation, vesting and eligibility to receive pension
benefits. You are eligible to receive pension benefits after completing different age and Years of Service
requirements.
If you are rehired following a termination of employment, your pre-termination Years of Credited Service will be
counted regardless of whether you were vested at the time of your termination.

Credited Service

You earn a year of Credited Service for each calendar year during which you are compensated for 2,000 or more
hours. Generally, you are credited with hours of employment for each compensated hour and for certain periods
of unpaid leaves. Proportional Credited Service is granted in years in which you have fewer than 2,000 hours of
employment.
Hours of Credited Service are also counted for uncompensated leaves of absence from CPMG. This includes up to
10 days of personal leave per calendar year; up to 90 days due to illness or other temporary disability, or for
medical research or advanced study approved under CPMG's leave policy if preceded by other Credited Service;
and for periods of qualified military service as required by law.
The plan also counts Hours of Credited Service for each hour for which you are on compensated or
uncompensated leaves of absence (credited in the same manner as described above for CPMG), as an employee of
any other Kaiser Permanente entity before your employment or reemployment with CPMG.

Years of Service and Credited Service for Leaves

In certain circumstances, the plan recognizes hours for periods of unpaid leave toward Years of Service and/or
Credited Service. For more information, contact CPMG Benefits.

How Your Benefit Is Calculated

The amount of your benefit will be based on a formula that includes:
· Your Highest Average Compensation (HAC) or Final Average Monthly Compensation, as applicable
· Your Years of Credited Service
· The plan multiplication factor in the formulas below
Important note for transition employees of the Washington Region: If, on February 1, 2017, you were a
transition employee as part of the acquisition of Group Health Cooperative and its affiliates, and subsequently
transferred to or were rehired by Kaiser Foundation Hospitals, or Kaiser Foundation Health Plan Inc., in another
Kaiser Permanente region, your eligible employment with Group Health Cooperative and its affiliates will count
when calculating your Service and Credited Service for your Kaiser Permanente Retirement Plan benefits in your
new region. Any benefit offset rules will continue to apply.

The Benefit Formula

The formula that is used to calculate your Single Life Annuity monthly pension benefit, assuming your benefit is
payable when you are age 65 for your lifetime, varies on whether you are a Physician, Executive, or Podiatrist.
(Certain grandfathered formulas may apply and are provided below.)

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 70
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Benefit Formula for Physicians

                                       4 percent of your Highest Average Compensation
                                                                         X

                                          Your years of Credited Service up to 20 years
                                                                         +

                                       2 percent of your Highest Average Compensation
                                                                         X

                                          Your years of Credited Service over 20 years
                                                                         ­

                                 Any applicable Pension Offset (see "Pension Offset Rules" )
All other forms of payment are based on this calculation. To help you understand how the formula works, here is
an explanation of the Highest Average Compensation and Monthly Compensation terms:

Highest Average Compensation
Your Highest Average Compensation (HAC) is the average of your Monthly Compensation for the highest
consecutive 36-month period of Monthly Compensation during the last 120 months before you terminate
employment with CPMG. If you have less than 36 months of compensated employment, your HAC generally is
the average monthly compensation for all of your months of compensated employment. Up to six months of leave
due to illness or temporary disability at your full-time rate are also included in calculating HAC.
Monthly Compensation
Your Monthly Compensation is one-half of your highest base rate of pay each month for services you perform for
CPMG or any other Kaiser Permanente Entity before you are employed by CPMG.

Benefit Formula for Executives and Podiatrists

                                 1.5 percent of your Final Average Monthly Compensation
                                                                         X

                                                    Your years of Credited Service
                                                                  ­

                                 Any applicable Pension Offset (see "Pension Offset Rules")
To help you understand how the formula works, here's an explanation of the Final Average Monthly
Compensation and Credited Service terms:

Final Average Monthly Compensation
Your Final Average Monthly Compensation (FAMC) is determined by looking at your monthly full-time
compensation rate for your last 120 months, or 10 years, of employment. Your monthly compensation rate is the
rate of base pay for the first compensated hour of each month multiplied by 173.33. Your highest monthly
compensation rates over a consecutive 60-month, or five-year, period -- typically the most recent 60-month
period -- are averaged to determine your FAMC. If you have fewer than 60 months of consecutive employment,
your FAMC is the average of the monthly compensation rates for all months of employment.
The maximum annual eligible pay set by the Internal Revenue Code (IRC) that may be considered for benefit
purposes for 2020 is $285,000. This amount may be indexed periodically for cost-of-living increases. In addition,
the IRC limits the annual benefit that may be paid to you from the plan.

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 71
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

How the Pension Calculation Works

Here is an example of how the formulas works:
Physicians
Dr. Smith retires in 2020 at age 65 with 35 years of Credited Service. Her Highest Average Compensation is
$10,000. Her monthly pension -- assuming she chooses the Life Only Annuity payment method -- is calculated
as follows:

                                      The first 20 years calculated at 4 percent = $8,000
                                                     Here is how that is calculated:
                                                              4 percent of HAC
                                                                         X
                                                                    20 years
                                                                         +

                                      The next 15 years calculated at 2 percent = $3,000
                                                     Here is how that is calculated:
                                                              2 percent of HAC
                                                                         X
                                                                    15 years

Dr. Smith's monthly pension will be $11,000, payable to her beginning at age 65 for her lifetime.
Please note: The actual date Dr. Smith can receive a benefit from the PPRP is subject to the terms described in
"When You Can Begin Your Benefit" below.
Executives and Podiatrists
Mr. Jones retires at age 65 with 35 years of Credited Service. His Final Average Monthly Compensation is
$15,000. His monthly pension -- assuming he chooses the Single Life Annuity payment method -- is calculated
as follows:

                                                     1.5 percent x $15,000 = $225
                                                                         X

                                                             35 years = $7,875
Mr. Jones's monthly pension will be $7,875, payable to him for his lifetime as a Single Life Annuity beginning at
age 65.
Please note: The actual date Mr. Jones can receive a benefit from the PPRP is subject to the terms described in
"When You Can Begin Your Benefit" below.

Pension Offset Rules

If you are vested in a benefit from another qualified defined benefit plan maintained by a Kaiser Permanente
entity, or from a Joint Labor Management Trust, and there are hours that are considered Credited Service under
both plans, your age 65 benefit under PPRP will be offset. Under the pension calculation formula, your PPRP
benefit will be offset by the age 65 benefit attributable to the period of overlapping Credited Service. You will have
to request your benefit from your earlier defined benefit plan separately.

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 72
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

For Washington Region transition employees who transfer to or are rehired in another Kaiser
Permanente region: If you were a transition employee as part of the acquisition of Group Health Cooperative
(GHC) and its affiliates, and then you transferred to or were rehired by Kaiser Foundation Hospitals or Kaiser
Foundation Health Plan, Inc., (KFHP/H) in another region, any pension benefit you may be eligible for under
your new position, will be offset by the sum of:
a) Any vested accrued benefit you are eligible for under a Kaiser Permanente Washington defined benefit plan as of
the date of your transfer or rehire, and
b) The actuarial equivalent of your balance as of January 31, 2017, in any defined contribution plans sponsored by
GHC and its affiliates.

Maximum Benefits

Federal tax law limits the annual benefit that the plan can pay to you. The Plan Administrator will notify you if
this limit affects the amount of your benefits.

When You Can Begin Your Benefit

If you are vested, you may qualify to begin receiving your benefit at Normal Retirement, Early Retirement,
Disability Retirement, In-Service Retirement, or Postponed Retirement. If you are vested and terminate your
employment with CPMG and all Kaiser Permanente entities before you qualify to begin receiving your benefit,
you will later qualify to begin receiving a Deferred Vested pension. Only one of these types of benefits is payable
from the plan, even if you satisfy the requirements for more than one type of benefit.

Normal Retirement

You will qualify for a Normal Retirement benefit if you terminate employment from CPMG when you turn age
65. Your Normal Retirement benefit is the monthly benefit calculated under the benefit formula. If you qualify,
you may elect to begin receiving your benefit on the first day of the month following your termination of
employment.

Early Retirement

You will qualify for Early Retirement if you terminate employment from CPMG and all other Kaiser Permanente
entities before the month in which you reach age 65 and you satisfy certain requirements at the time of your
termination:
· If you are a Physician, you must have 10 Years of Service.
· If you are an Executive or Podiatrist, you must be at least age 55 with 15 Years of Service, or your age and Years
of Service must equal 75.
If you qualify, you may elect to begin receiving an Early Retirement benefit on the last day of any month after you
meet these requirements.
Physicians
Your Early Retirement benefit is the same as your Normal Retirement benefit. However, if you elect to take a
distribution from the plan before you reach age 65, the amount of your monthly benefit will be actuarily reduced
based on your age when it begins, unless you qualify for Full Early Retirement. If you wait until you reach age 65
(the plan's Normal Retirement Age) to receive your benefit, it will not be reduced.

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 73
    RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Physician Full Early Retirement

You qualify for Full Early Retirement if you are a physician age 60 or older on your Benefit Commencement Date
and your age plus Years of Service at termination of employment equal 80 or more. If you meet these age and
Years of Service guidelines, no reduction will be applied to your benefit.

Executives and Podiatrists

Your Early Retirement benefit is the same as your Normal Retirement benefit. However, if you elect to begin
your Early Retirement benefit before you reach age 65, the amount of your monthly benefit will be reduced based
on your age on your Benefit Commencement Date. The following chart shows the percentage of your benefit
payable at earlier ages:

Your Age When Payments Begin  Percentage of Normal Retirement Payable
                     65                                to You

                                                        100%

64                            97%

63                            94%

62                            91%

61                            88%

60                            85%

59                            80%

58                            75%

57                            70%

56                            65%

55                            60%

Your benefit will be adjusted to reflect your actual age. For example, if you retire at age 62˝, your percentage will
be approximately 92.5 percent (halfway between the percentages for age 62 and age 63) of the normal pension.

If you are eligible and elect to begin receiving your benefit before age 55, your benefit will be reduced an
additional 5 percent per year for the period between your age on your Benefit Commencement Date and age 55.
In no event will your benefit be less than the actuarially reduced benefit reflecting your age on your Benefit
Commencement Date.

If you wait until you reach age 65 (the plan's Normal Retirement Age) to receive your benefit, it will not be
reduced.

Disability Retirement

You will qualify for a Disability Retirement benefit if you are eligible for disability benefits under Title II of the
Social Security Act and meet the following requirements:

CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 74
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

· You terminate employment from CPMG and all other Kaiser Permanente entities due to a disability that
  occurred while you were earning Years of Service.

· You have at least 5 or more Years of Service with CPMG.

· You are eligible to receive benefits under CPMG's Long-Term Disability plan.

· Your date of disability, as determined by the Social Security Administration, is on or before your termination
  date with CPMG and all other Kaiser Permanente entities.

Please note: Executives and Podiatrists are not eligible for Disability Retirement with respect to retirement
income accrued on or after September 1, 2010.

If you qualify, you may elect to begin receiving a Disability Retirement benefit on the first day of any month after
you meet these requirements. Your Disability Retirement benefit is calculated in the same manner as your
Normal Retirement benefit if you wait until age 65 to begin receiving your benefit.
However, if you elect to begin your Disability Retirement benefit before you reach age 65, the amount of your
monthly benefit will be reduced based on your Benefit Commencement Date unless you qualify for Full Early
Retirement. See "Early Retirement" above for the reductions that are applied to your benefit if payment begins
before 65. If you wait until you reach age 65 to receive your benefit, it will not be reduced.

Deferred Vested Pension

You will qualify for a Deferred Vested benefit if you terminate employment from CPMG after you become
vested, but before you qualify for Normal Retirement, Early Retirement or Disability Retirement. If you qualify,
you may elect to begin your Deferred Vested benefit on the first day of the month following the month in which
you reach age 65. Your Deferred Vested benefit is calculated in the same manner as your Normal Retirement
benefit if you wait until age 65 to begin receiving your benefit.

You may elect to begin receiving a reduced benefit before age 65 if you meet the Years of Service requirement for
Early Retirement when you terminate employment and later meet the age requirement. This means you will be
able to receive your benefit in accordance with the Early Retirement payment provisions.

See "Early Retirement" for the reductions that are applied to your benefit if payment begins before 65.

In-Service Retirement

You will qualify for In-Service Retirement if you are still employed by CPMG in an employee group eligible for
this benefit after you reach age 65. If you qualify, you may elect to start receiving your In-Service Retirement
benefit on the last day of any month following the month in which you reach age 65. Your In-Service Retirement
benefit is the same as your Normal Retirement benefit (or benefit earned to the date your benefit starts if later
than 65).

You may continue to earn additional benefits under the plan after you commence your In-Service Retirement
benefit if you continue your employment. However, any additional benefit that you may earn will not be payable
until you terminate your employment with CPMG. When you retire, your benefit will be recalculated under the
benefit formula based on your HAC/FAMC and total years of Credited Service at that time, and reduced by the
In-Service Retirement benefit you already received on an actuarially adjusted basis. While your final retirement
benefit will not be reduced below the In-Service retirement benefit you initially received, it is also unlikely to
increase. The form of payment you elected for In-Service Retirement will automatically apply to additional
benefits, if any, earned after your In-Service Retirement distribution.

Postponed Retirement

If you continue your employment with CPMG after you reach age 65, you can defer payment of your benefit
until you terminate your employment. At that time, you may elect to receive a Postponed Retirement benefit

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 75
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

beginning on the last day of any month after you terminate. Your Postponed Retirement benefit is a monthly
benefit for your lifetime generally equal to the greater of: (1) the actuarially adjusted Normal Retirement benefit
based on your HAC/FAMC and Years of Service (age 65); or (2) your benefit based on your HAC/FAMC and
years of Credited Service when you terminate employment. The amount you receive under certain forms of
payment may decrease as a result of your increased age when payment of the benefit begins.
Please note that federal tax law requires that you begin your Postponed Retirement benefit by April 1 after the year
in which you reach age 70˝, or, if later, the year in which you terminate your employment from the Kaiser
Permanente legal entity where you are working as of April 1 of the year after you attained 70˝.
If you have questions regarding the effect of your continued employment beyond age 65, contact CPMG Benefits.

Deferred Payment

You may elect to defer payment of your benefit beyond the earliest date you are entitled to begin receiving it. If
you defer your benefit beyond age 65, your benefit will be actuarially increased to reflect the delayed payment.
However, federal tax law requires that you begin your benefit by April 1 after the year in which you reach age
70˝, or, if later, the year in which you terminate your employment with CPMG.

Employees Who Transfer Among Kaiser Permanente Entities

The terms of the pension plans offered by Kaiser Permanente are not uniform. If you transfer among Kaiser
Permanente entities during your career, you might participate in different pension plans and the terms of those
plans may differ significantly. Keep this in mind and if you transfer, review the Summary Plan Description for the
terms of each pension plan.
If you transfer from CPMG to a position covered by another Kaiser Permanente defined benefit plan, your benefit
under PPRP will be based on your Credited Service as of your transfer date and will be calculated according to the
provisions of PPRP in effect when you transfer.

How Benefits Are Paid

You must complete and return a retirement commencement package and any other required forms or
documentation to receive your earned plan benefit. To begin the commencement process, visit the Kaiser
Permanente Retirement Center (KPRC) website at www.ibenefitcenter.com/kp,. You may also call the KPRC.
When you apply for your benefit, you can select the standard form of payment or one of the alternate forms of
payment. It is important to consider the available forms of payment carefully before making your selection. Once
you begin to receive benefits, you cannot change your form of payment. The form of payment you select may have
a number of tax implications. You should carefully consider your personal financial situation when selecting a form
of payment. The plan, its fiduciaries and its sponsoring employers cannot offer financial or tax advice on this
subject. For assistance, please consult a tax advisor or financial planner.

Standard Forms of Payment

If you are single: the standard form of payment is the Single Life Annuity.
If you are married: your spouse is entitled by federal law to receive benefits, so your standard form of payment is
the 50 percent Joint and Survivor Annuity. Therefore, you are legally required to obtain your spouse's consent to
elect other forms of payment. The consent must be in writing and notarized no more than 90 days before the
benefits begin.
Please see below for descriptions of these and the other available forms of payment under the plan.

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 76
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Available Forms of Payment

· Lump Sum: Under this option, you receive a one-time lump sum amount. After you receive the Lump Sum
  payment, there are no more payments due under the plan. The Lump Sum can be rolled over into a traditional
  IRA, Roth IRA or another employer's qualified plan, if that plan accepts rollovers.

· Single Life Annuity: Under this option, you receive a monthly pension benefit until your death. However, all
  pension payments stop when you die regardless of marital status. This is the standard form of payment if you
  are not married (as defined by federal law) on your Benefit Commencement Date.

· 50 percent, 662/3 percent, and 75 percent Joint and Survivor Annuities: Under this option, you receive a
  reduced monthly benefit until your death. If you die before your beneficiary, 50 percent, 662/3 percent, or 75
  percent (as elected by you) of the amount you receive will then be paid to your beneficiary as long as he or she
  lives. However, if your beneficiary dies before you, your monthly benefit will be reduced to the 50 percent, 662/3
  percent, or 75 percent survivor benefit for the rest of your lifetime after your beneficiary's death. This option
  requires the designation of one person as your beneficiary, and after your payments begin, you cannot change
  your beneficiary.

   The 50 percent Joint and Survivor Annuity is the standard form of payment if you are married (as defined by
   federal law). If you are married, you must select this form of payment with your spouse as your beneficiary
   unless your spouse consents to a different election. Your spouse's consent must be on the appropriate form and
   notarized.

   Once you begin receiving payments, you may not change your beneficiary. The monthly pension benefit you or
   your beneficiary receives under this option will be less than the monthly pension benefit under a Single Life
   Annuity because payments may continue after death. The actual difference depends on the percentage you elect
   (50 percent, 662/3 percent, or 75 percent) as well as the age difference between you and your beneficiary.

· 100 percent Joint and Survivor Annuity with 15-Year Guarantee Period and Pop-Up: Under this option,
  you receive a reduced monthly benefit until your death. If you die before your Joint and Survivor Annuity
  beneficiary, 100 percent of the monthly payment you received will then be paid to that beneficiary as long as he
  or she lives. However, if your Joint and Survivor Annuity beneficiary dies first, the monthly amount payable to
  you will "pop up" to the Single Life Annuity monthly amount for the duration of your life. If you and your
  Joint and Survivor Annuity beneficiary both die before the 180 months (15 years) of guaranteed payments are
  made, payments equal to the 100 percent Joint and Survivor Annuity monthly benefit will be made to a
  designated beneficiary until the expiration of the guaranteed payment period.

   If your designated beneficiary does not survive to the end of the guaranteed payment period, the present value of
   the remaining payments will be paid to that beneficiary's estate. This option requires the designation of both a
   Joint and Survivor Annuity beneficiary and a beneficiary for the guarantee period benefit. If you and your Joint
   and Survivor Annuity beneficiary die before 180 payments and there is no surviving designated beneficiary, the
   remaining payments will be made to your surviving spouse. If there is no surviving spouse, the present value of
   the remaining payments will be paid to your estate.

· 5-, 10-, 15- and 20-Year Certain and Life Annuity: Under this option, you receive a monthly pension benefit
  for your lifetime with payments that will be made for a period of at least 5, 10, 15, or 20 years, whichever you
  select. If you die before the end of the specified period, your designated beneficiary will receive the monthly
  payments for the remainder of the specified period.

   If your designated beneficiary dies before the end of the specified period, the present value of the remaining
   monthly benefits will be paid in accordance with the plan.

   For example, if you elect the 10-year option and die after receiving payments for only six years, your beneficiary
   would receive monthly payments for the remaining four years. If you live longer than 10 years, payments will

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 77
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

   continue to you for as long as you live, but there are no payments to your beneficiary after your death. If your
   beneficiary dies after you, but before all the fixed-period payments have been made, the remaining fixed-period
   payments will be made in a lump sum to your beneficiary's estate.

   The monthly amount paid to you under this option will be less than you would receive under a Single Life
   Annuity because of the possibility that payments will continue after your death. The actual difference depends
   on your age at retirement and the length of the specified period. Unlike a Joint and Survivor Annuity, you can
   change your beneficiary for this form of payment after your payments begin.

· Bifurcated Payment: Under this option, you elect to divide your accrued benefit into two equal portions,
  receiving one portion as a lump sum and the remaining portion of your retirement benefit as either a Single Life
  Annuity, a 50 percent Joint and Survivor Annuity, or a 100 percent Joint and Survivor Annuity with 15-Year
  Guarantee Period and Pop-Up. The Benefit Commencement Date for each portion of the accrued benefit must
  be the same. The amount of the distribution payable with respect to each portion of the accrued benefit is
  determined in accordance with the method for calculating the amount of a distribution payable in that form of
  payment as if that portion were your entire accrued benefit.

Additional Forms of Payments for Executives and Podiatrists
· Fixed Monthly Installments: Under this option, you receive a fixed number of monthly payments, and then

  all payments stop. You may elect to receive installments for 60, 120, 180, 240, or 360 months, or any months
  up to 360. If you die after your payments stop because you have received the fixed number of monthly
  payments, there will be no benefit paid to any beneficiary. If you die before you receive the fixed number of
  monthly payments, your surviving designated beneficiary will receive monthly installments for the remainder of
  the fixed period.

· Level Income Annuity Option at Age 62, 65 or your Social Security Normal Retirement Age: Under
  this option, you receive an increased monthly payment during your lifetime until age 62, age 65 or your Social
  Security Normal Retirement Age (SSNRA), as you elect. Thereafter, it provides a reduced monthly payment for
  your life in order to provide an approximate level retirement benefit when the reduced monthly payment is
  combined with your estimated benefit from Social Security. This option is only available if your requested
  Benefit Commencement Date is before the leveling age. The leveling age is the age at which the payment
  decreases. The first decreased payment will be the first month following the leveling age. The plan offers the
  following leveling ages: 62, 65, or SSNRA.

· 5-, 10-, 15- and 20-Year Certain and Life Annuity with Level Income Option at Age 62, 65 or your
  Social Security Normal Retirement Age: Under this option, you receive an increased monthly payment
  during your lifetime until age 62, age 65 or your Social Security Normal Retirement Age (SSNRA), as you elect.
  Thereafter, it provides a reduced monthly payment payable for your life in order to provide an approximate level
  retirement benefit when the reduced monthly payment is combined with your estimated benefit received from
  Social Security. If you die during the period you elect (5, 10, 15 or 20 years), your beneficiary will receive the
  remaining payments until all of the specified payments have been made. This option is only available if your
  Benefit Commencement Date is before the leveling age. The leveling age is the age at which the payment
  decreases. The first decreased payment will be the first month following the leveling age. The plan offers the
  following leveling ages: 62, 65, or SSNRA.

The amount payable under each method is determined using actuarial assumptions and the interest rate specified
by the plan. You will be provided with estimates of the amounts payable under each of the different methods as
part of your commencement package.

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 78
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Domestic Partners

Although CPMG recognizes domestic partnerships, the federal government, which regulates many of our benefit
plans, does not. Thus, wherever the terms "married" and "spouse" are used in this Summary Plan Description
(SPD), they mean a couple that has entered into a legal marriage.

If You Die

If You Die While Still Employed

Physicians

If you die after you are eligible for a benefit under this plan and after you are vested, but before you make a written
election to begin your benefits, your beneficiary will be eligible for a survivor benefit from the plan. If your
beneficiary is your spouse, this benefit is payable no later than when you would have turned age 65. Your spouse
may elect to begin payments when you would have been eligible for early retirement, and may elect a lump sum or
a lifetime monthly survivor benefit from the plan. The amount of your beneficiary's benefit will be your accrued
benefit as of your date of death. If your beneficiary is not your spouse, payment is made in a single sum in the
month following your death.

Executives and Podiatrists

If Your Beneficiary Is Your Spouse or Designated Domestic Partner
If you die while still employed at Kaiser Permanente and after you are vested, but before you make a written
election to begin your benefits, your spouse or designated domestic partner will be eligible for a lifetime monthly
survivor benefit from the plan. This benefit is payable to your spouse when you would have turned 65. Your spouse
may also elect to begin payments when you would have been eligible for Early Retirement, but cannot defer
payment later than April 1 following the year you would have reached age 70˝. Domestic partners must begin
receiving a distribution before the first anniversary of your death.
The amount of your spouse's or designated domestic partner's benefit will be the same as if you had selected the 66
2/3 percent Joint and Survivor Annuity form of payment and died on the day of your spouse's Benefit
Commencement Date.
In order to designate your domestic partner for pre-retirement survivor benefits, you must complete a Designation
of Domestic Partner for Pre-Retirement Survivor Benefits form. This form is different than the form that is
required to add your domestic partner to your medical and/or dental benefits. If you would like to designate your
domestic partner for this benefit, please contact CPMG Benefits for the appropriate form. If you do not designate
your domestic partner, a pre-retirement survivor benefit is payable to your domestic partner if you qualified for
this benefit and if proof of domestic partnership is provided, such as a copy of a certified domestic partner
registration from a state or local government.

If Your Beneficiary Is Not Your Spouse or Domestic Partner
If your beneficiary is not your spouse or designated domestic partner, and you die while still employed at Kaiser
Permanente and after you are vested, but before you make a written election to begin your benefits, your
beneficiary will receive a lump sum payment on the last day of the month following your death. The benefit will
be the actuarial equivalent of your accrued benefit as of that date.

If You Die After You Terminate Employment But Before Benefits Commence

Physicians

If you die after you terminate employment and after you are vested, but before you make a written election to
begin your benefits, your beneficiary will be eligible for a survivor benefit from the plan. If your beneficiary is your

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 79
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

spouse, this benefit is payable no later than when you would have turned age 65. Your spouse may elect to begin
payments when you would have been eligible for Early Retirement, and may elect a lump sum or a lifetime
monthly survivor benefit from the plan. The amount of your beneficiary's benefit will be your accrued benefit as
of your date of death. If your beneficiary is not your spouse, payment is made in a single sum in the month
following your death.

Executives and Podiatrists

If Your Beneficiary Is Your Spouse or Designated Domestic Partner
If you die after you terminate employment and after you are vested, but before you make a written election to
begin your benefits, your spouse or designated domestic partner will be eligible for a lifetime monthly survivor
benefit from the plan. This benefit is payable to your spouse when you would have turned 65. Your spouse may
also choose to elect to begin payments any time after you would have been eligible for Early Retirement, but
cannot defer payment later than April 1 following the year you would have reached age 70˝. Domestic partners
must begin receiving a distribution before the first anniversary your death.
The amount of your spouse's or designated domestic partner's benefit will be the same as if you had selected the 50
percent Joint and Survivor Annuity form of payment and died on the day of your spouse's Benefit
Commencement Date.

If Your Beneficiary Is Not Your Spouse or Domestic Partner
If your beneficiary is not your spouse or designated domestic partner, and you die after you terminate employment
and after you are vested, but before you make a written election to begin your benefits, your beneficiary will
receive a lump sum payment on the last day of the month following your death. The benefit will be the actuarial
equivalent of your accrued benefit as of that date.

If You Die After Benefits Commence

If you die after you have made a written election to have your benefits begin and you elected a form of payment
that provides for payments after death, benefits will continue to your beneficiary pursuant to that form of
payment. If you made a written election of a form of payment that does not provide for payments after death, no
additional payments will be made after your death. Special rules apply in the event you are married and you are
survived by your spouse.

Minimum Distribution Requirement

You are required by law to take a minimum distribution of your benefit by April 1 of the calendar year following
the year in which you reach age 70˝ or retire, whichever is later. All of the plan's forms of payment are designed
to meet the minimum distribution requirements. Minimum distributions are not eligible to be rolled into an IRA
or another tax-qualified retirement plan.

If You Are Rehired

If you are rehired by Kaiser Permanente and are scheduled to work 20 or more hours per week, or actually work at
least 1,000 Hours of Service in a calendar year, any retirement benefits you are currently receiving from the plan
will be suspended. If you are scheduled to work less than 20 hours per week and you work fewer than 1,000 Hours
of Service in a year, your benefits will continue. Your Years of Service and Credited Service earned during the time
you are re-employed are used to determine any additional benefits when you terminate employment again. Your
future benefits will be reduced based on any benefits already distributed to you.
If you leave and then return to work at CPMG as an eligible employee, you participate in the plan on your date of
rehire, as long as you were a participant before your original termination date. If you are not employed as an

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 80
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

eligible employee on your rehire date, you will again become a participant only after you again become an eligible
employee.

Unclaimed Benefit Process

You are required to keep your most current address on file with CPMG Benefits. If you cannot be located within
90 days of the date your benefit is required to be paid, your benefit will be forfeited and used by the plan. If you
later return to claim your benefit, it will be deemed payable as of the required payment date.

Assignment of Benefits

Generally, your benefits under the plan cannot be assigned, given away, transferred, or pledged in any way. There
are some exceptions, such as a Qualified Domestic Relations Order (QDRO) and qualified federal tax liens. For
details of this provision, see the Legal and Administrative Information section.

Tax Considerations

CPMG intends that the plan be tax qualified. With tax-qualification, your accruals under the plan are not
currently taxable to you and you are taxed when you actually receive pension payments from the plan. Such
payments will generally be taxable as ordinary income in the year received. However, the tax rules which apply to
this plan are complex and apply differently to each individual. CPMG does not guarantee the tax treatment of the
plan or any distributions from the plan.
The Plan Administrator will provide you with a written notice at the time you become eligible to receive a
distribution of benefits, which describes in general the tax consequences of the available distribution options. The
Plan Administrator cannot advise you on your taxes. You should seek qualified tax advice regarding your own
specific situation before making a decision as to the desired method of distribution. You also may wish to review
IRS Publication 575 " Pension and Annuity Income," available free of charge online or at your local IRS office.

Potential Loss of Benefits

The plan is intended to provide you with a retirement benefit. However, some individuals may not qualify for a
benefit and others may lose a benefit even if they once qualified. You should be aware that the following are some,
but not all, of the possible reasons you may not receive part or all of a benefit:
· If you do not meet the requirements for eligibility to participate, you will not be entitled to any benefit.
· If you terminate employment before becoming vested, you may lose any benefit you have earned.
· If all or a portion of your benefits are awarded to an alternate payee pursuant to a QDRO, you will not receive

  your entire benefit.
· If the plan is terminated with insufficient assets to provide your benefit, and if the PBGC does not guarantee all

  of your benefit, then your benefit may be reduced or may be lost altogether.
· If the plan should be disqualified by the IRS, contributions made to the plan and earnings on plan assets may

  result in current taxable income to you.
· If the plan should overpay any benefits to you, the Plan Administrator has the right to offset the overpayment

  against future benefit payments to you, to recover the overpayment directly from you, or to use any other
  methods to recover the overpayment.
· If the plan is less than 80 percent funded, then you will be provided with a notice of the plan's funding level and
  certain restrictions on amendments, benefits and accruals may apply.

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021 | Page 81
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

For More Information

For more information about your plan benefit or to obtain a pension estimate, contact CPMG Benefits.

Colorado Permanente Medical Group Cash Balance Plan

The Cash Balance Plan is a tax-qualified defined benefit plan available to eligible CPMG a Physician, Executive,
or Podiatrist hired on or after July 1, 2016. This plan, which is fully funded by CPMG, allows qualified
participants to earn annual Pay Credits and Interest Credits over time. For detailed information about this
retirement plan, please refer to Appendix B: Cash Balance Plan.
Please note: Current PPRP participants as well as rehired CPMG employees who previously participated in the
PPRP are not eligible for the Cash Balance Plan. They will remain in the PPRP as long as they are eligible.

Colorado Permanente Cash or Deferred Profit Sharing Plan

The Colorado Permanente Cash or Deferred Profit Sharing Plan is a defined contribution retirement savings
plan. For detailed information about this retirement plan, please refer to Appendix C: Colorado Permanente
Medical Group Cash or Deferred Profit Sharing Plan.

Retiree Medical Benefits

CPMG offers retiree medical benefits to employees who meet certain age and years of service requirements as
active employees, and who meet other eligibility requirements as described below.

Who Is Eligible

To be eligible for retiree medical coverage, you must be part of a Physician, Executive, or Podiatrist of CPMG and
retire under the Early, Normal, Disability, or Postponed Retirement provisions of the Permanente Physicians
Retirement Plan (PPRP), even if you qualify only for the CPMG Cash Balance Plan.

When Benefits Begin

The start date of your retiree medical benefits is determined by the eligibility requirements and applicable Years of
Service noted below:

Physicians

Early Retirement: If you qualify for Early Retirement at age 55 with 15 or more Years of Service, you and your
eligible dependents are provided retiree medical coverage when you turn age 65. Participation in Medicare is
required. You pay for Part B of Medicare and assign benefits to Kaiser Permanente by enrolling in Kaiser
Permanente Senior Advantage (KPSA).
Full Early Retirement: If you qualify for Full Early Retirement at age 60, you and your eligible dependents are
provided retiree medical coverage and Supplemental Medical coverage until you turn age 65, at which time
participation in Medicare is required in order to continue coverage. You pay for Part B of Medicare and assign
benefits to Kaiser Permanente by enrolling in KPSA.
Normal Retirement: If you qualify for Normal Retirement at age 65 with 10 or more Years of Service, you and
your eligible dependents are provided retiree medical coverage when you retire. You pay for Part B of Medicare
and assign benefits to Kaiser Permanente by enrolling in KPSA.

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021| Page 82
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Executives and Podiatrists

If you were hired before January 1, 1985: If you qualify for Early Retirement at age 55 with 15 or more Years
of Service, or when your age plus Years of Service equals at least 75, you and your eligible dependents are provided
retiree medical coverage and Supplemental Medical coverage effective the first day of the month following your
retirement date. Participation in Medicare is required once you turn 65. You pay for Part B of Medicare and assign
benefits to Kaiser Permanente by enrolling in KPSA.
If you were hired on or after January 1, 1985: If you qualify for Early Retirement at age 55 with 15 or more
Years of Service, or when your age plus Years of Service equals at least 75, you and your eligible dependents are
provided retiree medical coverage when you turn age 65. Participation in Medicare is required. You pay for Part B
of Medicare and assign benefits to Kaiser Permanente by enrolling in KPSA.
Normal Retirement: If you qualify for Normal Retirement at age 65 with 15 or more Years of Service, you and
your eligible dependents are provided retiree medical coverage when you retire. You pay for Part B of Medicare
and assign benefits to Kaiser Permanente by enrolling in KPSA.

If You Retire After Age 65

If you meet the age and Years of Service eligibility requirements (see above), you and your eligible dependents who
are enrolled in Kaiser Permanente-sponsored medical coverage when you retire will be offered retiree medical
benefits effective the first day of the month following your retirement date.

Your Retiree Medical Coverage

As a retired or disabled Physician, Executive, or Podiatrist, you, your spouse or domestic partner, and eligible
dependent children will receive medical and Supplemental Medical coverage that is similar to the coverage received
by active Physicians, Executives, or Podiatrists at the time your retiree medical coverage begins.
If your retiree medical coverage begins on or after age 65, you will receive Medicare-coordinated coverage. If you
are covered under Kaiser Permanente Senior Advantage (KPSA) but your eligible dependents are not at least age
65 and Medicare-eligible, your dependents will be covered under the KFHP medical plan even though you are
covered under KPSA.
If you retire before you are eligible for Medicare and are covered by the KFHP medical plan, your eligible
dependents will be covered under the same plan as you are.
If there are any changes to the coverage provided to active Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists, your retiree
medical coverage will change as well.

Your Costs

Kaiser Permanente pays the cost of your retiree medical benefit premiums. You share the costs for medical
coverage through copayments for certain services.
If you choose to extend retiree medical benefits to your domestic partner and his or her eligible dependents, the
benefits provided may result in taxable income to you. Refer to the Flexible Benefits section for a description of
domestic partner benefits.

How to Enroll

You and your eligible spouse or domestic partner must enroll according to plan rules in order to receive retiree
medical benefits.
To begin your retiree medical benefits enrollment process, contact CPMG Benefits at least 90 days prior to your
eligibility. They will also attempt to contact you at your last known address. It is important to keep your address

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021| Page 83
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

current with CPMG Benefits so that they can contact you when you are eligible to commence benefits and for you
to receive any applicable benefit updates.
Ninety days before you and any eligible dependents become eligible for Medicare (typically at age 65), please
follow these steps. You and your Medicare-eligible dependents must complete all four steps to enroll in retiree
medical benefits:
1. Enroll in Medicare Parts A and B by contacting the Social Security Administration. Visit www.medicare.gov.
2. Enroll in a retiree medical plan through CPMG Benefits.
3. After you complete Step 2, CPMG Benefits will send you a Senior Advantage Group Enrollment Form to
complete and return. Be sure to follow the instructions on the form.
Once you've done so, CPMG Benefits will provide you with additional instructions on how to commence your
benefits.

Medicare Assignment

Once you become eligible for Medicare, your retiree coverage will be integrated with Medicare. You and your
spouse or domestic partner, when eligible, must enroll in all applicable parts of Medicare (including Parts A and
B), and enroll in Kaiser Permanente Senior Advantage. If you do not enroll in Medicare and sign over your
Medicare by enrolling in the Kaiser Permanente Senior Advantage group plan, your retiree medical benefits will be
terminated. If you move to an area where there is no Kaiser Permanente Senior Advantage plan available, please
contact the KPRC.

Kaiser Permanente will automatically assign your Part D for you when you enroll in the Kaiser Permanente Senior
Advantage group plan; a specific assignment will not be required by you. If you assign Part D coverage to another
provider, Medicare will notify Kaiser Permanente and your retiree medical coverage may be terminated.

You will be responsible for paying the Medicare Part B premiums. You will also be responsible for paying any
Medicare surcharges.

Important: If you live in a Kaiser Permanente Senior Advantage Service Area, you must enroll

in a Kaiser Permanente Senior Advantage group plan in order to receive employer-provided coverage.

If You Move Outside Your Home Region

If you move outside of your home region as a retiree, the medical benefits available to you may differ depending
on where you move. Your home region is defined as the Kaiser Permanente region from which you retired and
became eligible for retiree medical benefits. It is important for you to contact CPMG Benefits at least two months
before your move to alert them of your new address, for information on the retiree medical coverage available to
you in your new location, and to ensure that your new retiree medical benefits start on time.

If You Move to Another Kaiser Permanente Region

The benefits you receive if you move to another region may be different than the benefits offered in your home
region; however, you are still required to assign your Medicare benefits to Kaiser Permanente once you become
eligible for Medicare.

If You Live Outside any Kaiser Permanente Medicare Service Area

If you move to a zip code outside of the Kaiser Permanente Medicare service area for longer than 90 days, you will
not be eligible for the Kaiser Permanente Senior Advantage Plan.
Please contact CPMG Benefits for information on the retiree medical benefits available to you if you move out of
area.

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021| Page 84
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Retiree Medical Coverage for Survivors

After You Retire

In the event of your death during retirement, your spouse or domestic partner and eligible children -- if they were
enrolled in medical coverage on your last day as an employee -- may continue or begin benefits, based on the
eligibility requirements and applicable Years of Service noted below.

Please note: Coverage for your spouse or domestic partner continues until he or she remarries, enters a new
domestic partner relationship, or dies. Coverage for your dependent children continues until they no longer meet
the eligibility requirements.

Physicians

Early Retirement: Eligible survivors are provided retiree medical coverage at age 65. Survivor pays Part B of
Medicare and assigns benefits to Kaiser Permanente by enrolling in KPSA.

Full Early Retirement: Retiree medical coverage for eligible survivors is deferred to when you would have reached
age 60. Medical and Supplemental Medical coverage is provided to survivors up to age 65, at which time
participation in Medicare is required. Survivor pays for Part B of Medicare and assigns benefits to Kaiser
Permanente by enrolling in KPSA.

Normal Retirement: Medical and Supplemental Medical coverage is provided to survivor up to age 65, at which
time participation in Medicare is required. Survivor pays for Part B of Medicare and assigns benefits to Kaiser
Permanente by enrolling in KPSA.

Executives and Podiatrists

If you qualify for Early Retirement and were hired before January 1, 1985: Your eligible survivors may
continue medical and Supplemental Medical coverage, or begin coverage, based on your eligibility. At age 65,
your survivor pays for Part B of Medicare and assigns benefits to Kaiser Permanente by enrolling in KPSA.

If you qualify for Early Retirement and were hired on or after January 1, 1985: Your eligible survivors may
continue medical and Supplemental Medical coverage, or begin coverage, based on your eligibility. At age 65, your
survivor pays for Part B of Medicare and assigns benefits to Kaiser Permanente by enrolling in KPSA.

Normal Retirement: Medical and Supplemental Medical coverage is provided to survivor and eligible dependents
up to age 65, at which time participation in Medicare is required. Your survivor pays for Part B of Medicare and
assigns benefits to Kaiser Permanente by enrolling in KPSA.

Before You Retire

If you die while actively employed, and after becoming eligible for retiree medical benefits, your spouse or
domestic partner and eligible children may continue benefits (or begin benefits, based on when you would have
been eligible). Survivor benefits will end if your spouse or domestic partner remarries or enters a new domestic
partner relationship. Eligibility for your children will end at age 26. Please note that your disabled dependents age
26 or older will lose eligibility for benefits in the event of your death.

Dependents who lose eligibility may continue coverage at their own expense under COBRA or purchase coverage
through the Health Insurance Marketplace. Contact CPMG Benefits or refer to the Health Care section for an
explanation of COBRA.

When Benefits End

Your retiree medical benefits will end upon your death or if you fail to assign your Medicare benefits to Kaiser
Permanente as required. For more information, refer to "Medicare Assignment."

If your benefits end due to death, benefits may continue for your eligible dependents. Refer to "Retiree Medical
Coverage for Survivors."

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021| Page 85
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

If you change your status after retirement (e.g., legal separation, divorce, adoption, or domestic partnership) you
must report your change in status to CPMG Benefits within 31 days in order to have your level of benefits
adjusted.

Retiree Life Insurance

Kaiser Permanente provides Retiree Life insurance coverage when you retire.
If eligible, you will be automatically enrolled in employer-paid retiree life insurance.
When you retire, you will need to name a beneficiary to receive payment of your life insurance benefits in the
event of your death. If you had designated beneficiaries for your life insurance as an active employee, please note
that these beneficiary designations will not carry over to Retiree Life insurance. You will need to re-designate
your beneficiaries for this benefit. Please contact CPMG Benefits for more information.

Who Is Eligible

You are eligible for Retiree Life insurance if you meet the following requirements when you terminate
employment:

Physicians

Retiree Life insurance coverage will be provided for those physicians meeting the Early Retirement rule as stated
under the PPRP plan and who are carrying the Basic Life insurance plan through the CPMG Benefits Program at
the time of retirement.

Executives and Podiatrists

If you retire under the Early, Normal, Disability, or Postponed Retirement provisions of the PPRP, you are eligible
for retiree life insurance coverage, according to the provisions below.

How Retiree Life Insurance Works

Physicians

CPMG will continue to pay the same amount for your life insurance during your retirement as it paid at the
commencement of your retirement; however, your coverage will be gradually reduced because the cost of life
insurance increases with age.

Executives and Podiatrists

If you take a Deferred Vested retirement, you may convert your coverage to an individual policy at your own
expense, but you will not be eligible for retiree life insurance coverage. Accidental Death and Dismemberment
insurance terminates upon retirement.
If you were hired on or after January 1, 1985: If you were enrolled in the Employee Life insurance plan on
December 31, 1995, the amount of life insurance on the day you retire will be two times your annual salary at
retirement. One month following your retirement, your coverage will decrease, i.e., taper, 1 percent per month for
75 months. The minimum coverage will be $2,000, or 25 percent of the amount at the start of tapering,
whichever amount is higher.
If you were not enrolled in the Basic (Contributory) life insurance plan on December 31, 1995, your coverage will
start at $50,000. One month following your retirement, your coverage will decrease, i.e., taper, 1 percent per
month for 75 months until you reach the final level of 25 percent of the initial amount at retirement.

If you were hired before January 1, 1985: The amount of life insurance on the day you retire will be one times
or three times your annual salary at retirement, depending on your Employee Life insurance election while you
were employed. One month following your retirement, your coverage will decrease, i.e., taper, 1 percent per

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021| Page 866
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

month for 75 months. The minimum coverage will be $2,000 or 25 percent of the amount at the start of
tapering, whichever amount is higher.

Imputed Income

According to Internal Revenue Service (IRS) regulation, the premium cost of employer-paid Retiree Life coverage
in excess of $50,000 is considered imputed income. Each year that you remain covered, an applicable amount of
imputed income will be included as taxable income on your Form W-2.

Cost of Coverage

The premium for your Retiree Life insurance coverage is employer-paid.

Conversion Privilege

You have the option to convert amounts of your life insurance lost due to retirement. You may convert your life
insurance coverage to an individual policy within 31 days of your retirement. You may also convert your
supplemental life coverage.
You may not convert your coverage retroactively. Contact CPMG Benefits for an explanation of your life
insurance conversion rights.

When Coverage Ends

Your retiree life insurance coverage ends if you return to work with any Kaiser Permanente entity and become
eligible for benefits based on your work schedule.
When you resume your retirement, your Retiree Life insurance coverage may be reinstated depending on your last
position, employment status, and employee group.
If you die, your surviving spouse or domestic partner's coverage will continue until remarriage or death or until
entry into a new domestic partner relationship, or whenever a domestic partner is no longer your domestic partner.
Your surviving dependents' coverage will continue until they no longer meet dependent eligibility requirements.
If you change your status after retirement (e.g., marriage, adoption, civil union, or domestic partner) your change
in status must be reported to CPMG Benefits within 31 days in order to have your level of coverage adjusted.

                              CPMG | Physicians, Executives, and Podiatrists | January 2021| Page 877
Disputes, Claims, and Appeals

This section of the SPD describes the dispute process and how to file a claim for your health and welfare
retirement benefits, retirement savings benefits, and/or retirement health benefits. In addition, you will find
information on how to appeal a benefit claim determination.
