                                                 APPENDIX A

                                          CLAIMS PROCEDURES
                                                     UNDER

                     COLORADO PERMANENTE MEDICAL GROUP, P.C.
                                          CASH BALANCE PLAN
                                             As of January 1, 2017

         1.01 Claims

                  1.01-1 All claims for benefits must be made in writing to the Claims
Administrator appointed by the Committee to decide claims (and in the absence of any such
appointment the Committee). The Claims Administrator will approve or deny each claim and
will notify the claimant no later than 90 days after the receipt of the written claim. If an
extension of time for processing the claim is required due to special circumstances, written
notice of the extension will be provided to the claimant before the termination of the initial 90-
day period. In no event will the extension exceed a period of 90 days from the end of the initial
period. The extension notice will indicate the special circumstances requiring an extension of
time and the date by which the Claims Administrator expects to issue a benefit determination.

                  1.01-2 If a claim is denied, the claimant will be advised in writing of:

                               (a) The specific reasons for denial;

                               (b) Specific reference to pertinent Plan provisions on which the
                  denial is based;

                               (c) A description of any additional material or information
                  necessary for the claimant to perfect the claim and an explanation of why the
                  material or information is necessary; and

                               (d) An explanation of the Plan's claim review procedure, and the
                  time limits applicable to such procedures, including that claimant may have the
                  claim reviewed by the Committee and that the claimant has the right to bring a
                  civil action under ERISA Section 502(a) following an adverse determination on
                  review.

         1.02 Appeals

                  1.02-1 A claimant or claimant's authorized representative may request a
review of a denied claim if such request is filed within 90 days of the date of the written
notification of the denial. In connection with the appeal, the claimant or the claimant's counsel
may request free of charge (a) reasonable access to and copies of pertinent documents and
records to the extent not inconsistent with other Participants' and Beneficiaries' privacy rights,
(b) other information relevant to the claim (as determined in accordance with applicable
Department of Labor Regulations), and (c) the opportunity to submit any statements, documents,
records or written argument in support of the claim.

90523757.2 0057444-00001  A-1
                                                                Appendix B

             (a) The Committee will process the appeal as follows:

                      (1) If the Committee holds regularly scheduled meetings at
             least quarterly, a decision upon review of the claim will be made by
             the Committee at a regularly scheduled meeting. If the request for
             review is received at least 30 days prior to the next regularly scheduled
             meeting, a determination will be made at that meeting. If the request
             for review is received less than 30 days before the date of the next
             regularly scheduled meeting, a determination will be made by the date
             of the second regularly scheduled meeting following the receipt of the
             request for review. If special circumstances require a further extension
             of time for processing, a benefit determination will be made not later
             than the third regularly scheduled meeting after the receipt of the
             request for review. If such an extension is required, the Committee
             shall provide the claimant with written notice of the extension,
             describing the special circumstances requiring extension and the date
             as of which the benefit determination will be made before the
             commencement of the extension. The Committee shall notify the
             claimant within five days of its determination.

                      (2) If the Committee does not hold regularly scheduled
             meetings at least quarterly, the Committee will notify the claimant of
             its determination on review within a reasonable time not longer than
             60 days after the Plan received the request for review unless an
             extension of time is required for a hearing or other special
             circumstances. The Committee will notify a claimant in writing of the
             need for any extension before the end of the initial 60 days, and no
             extension will be longer than another 60 days after the initial period.
             Any notice of extension will indicate the special circumstances
             requiring the extension and the date by which a decision is expected.

                      (3) In performing the review, the Committee will take into
             account all comments, documents, records and other information
             submitted by the claimant relating to the claim without regard to
             whether such information was submitted or considered in the initial
             benefit determination.

             (b) The decision on review will be in writing and will provide the
following information if the appeal is denied:

                      (1) The specific reason or reasons for the denial;

                      (2) Reference to the specific provision or provisions of the
             Plan or other documents governing the Plan on which the denial is
             based;

90523757.2 0057444-00001  A-2
                                                                             Appendix B

                                        (3) A statement that the claimant is entitled to receive,
                               upon request and free of charge, reasonable access to, and copies of,
                               all documents, records or other information (as determined in
                               accordance with applicable Department of Labor Regulations) to the
                               claimant's request for review; and

                                        (4) A statement of the claimant's right to bring a civil
                               action under ERISA Section 502(a).

                               (c) The decision of the Committee on any request for review shall
                  be final and conclusive upon all persons, except as judicially ordered.

         1.03 Exhaustion Requirement

                  1.03-1 The claims and review procedures described in this Appendix must be
exhausted before a claimant may bring a legal action in court relating to the claim; however, if
the Claims Administrator or Committee (as applicable) fails to render a decision within the time
limits set forth in Sections 1.01 and 1.02, the claimant shall be deemed to have exhausted his or
her remedies under this Appendix. This paragraph applies if a claimant does not receive
payment of the benefits the claimant believes he or she is entitled to receive under the Plan or has
any other grievance with respect to his or her benefits under the Plan (including but not limited
to a redetermination of benefits, or a determination of current or future rights under the Plan).

         1.04 Time Limitation and Forum Selection

                  1.04-1 Nothing in this Section excuses a person from the exhaustion
requirement described in Section 1.03.

                               (a) Any claim for benefits under the Plan, pursuant to this Section,
                  must be filed with the Plan Administrator by the latest of:

                                        (1) Two years following the date a Participant has a
                               Termination of Employment;

                                        (2) Two years following the date the Participant is provided
                               with written notice (including electronic information made available to
                               the Participant by the Plan) of the Participant's Vested status and/or
                               the components of benefit payment as applicable to the claim; and

                                        (3) December 31, 2017.

                               (b) If the Plan Administrator fails to timely pay a claimant's
                  retirement benefit as of the claimant's Benefit Starting Date, then the claimant
                  shall have one year from the claimant's Benefit Starting Date (or, if later, the
                  deadline described in subsection (a)) to file a claim solely with regard to the
                  failure to timely pay the claimant's retirement benefit. Any claim submitted after
                  the period described in subsection (a) expires shall be precluded, including claims

90523757.2 0057444-00001  A-3
                                                               Appendix B

that relate to the calculation of the retirement benefit, the Benefit Starting Date, or
any other claim, unless that claim relates solely to:

                      (1) The failure to timely pay the previously determined
             amount of the retirement benefit;

                      (2) The form of payment of the retirement benefit, and/or

                      (3) The adjustment to the claimant's retirement benefit for
             commencement before Normal Retirement Date.

             (c) The Committee, in its sole discretion, will determine whether
any limitation in (a) or (b) has been exceeded.

             (d) No legal action (whether in law, in equity or otherwise) shall
be commenced seeking judicial review of a decision under this Appendix more
than one year after the later of the date of the initial denial of the claim, or if a
timely request for appeal of the denial has been made, the date the Committee
denies the claimant's appeal.

             (e) Any legal action (whether in law, in equity or otherwise) must
be brought in the U.S. District Court of Colorado (Denver) where the Plan is
administered.

             (f) The Committee shall be an agent for service of process on the
Plan at the Company's address.

                                 QUESTIONS AND ANSWERS ABOUT
   THE CASH OR DEFERRED PROFIT SHARING PLAN AND TRUST AGREEMENT

                                                         OF
                      COLORADO PERMANENTE MEDICAL GROUP, P.C.

                           For Physician Employees, Podiatrist Employees, and
                          Officers of Colorado Permanente Medical Group, P.C.
                   Effective Date of this Summary Plan Description: January 1, 2018

Active/47385346.1
                                                                               Appendix C

                                QUESTIONS AND ANSWERS ABOUT

THE CASH OR DEFERRED PROFIT SHARING PLAN AND TRUST AGREEMENT
                     OF COLORADO PERMANENTE MEDICAL GROUP, P.C.

                 Colorado Permanente Medical Group, P.C. (the "Medical Group") maintains this
profit-sharing plan for the exclusive benefit of its employees and their beneficiaries. To acquaint
you with the plan, the following questions and answers summarize the major provisions of the plan
and trust. If you find that not every question concerning the plan is answered, the plan and trust
document itself is available for your examination at the office of the Plan Administrator. The actual
text of the plan governs all matters.

         1. What is the purpose of the plan?

                 The purpose of the Cash or Deferred Profit Sharing Plan and Trust Agreement is
to provide a systematic and advantageous method of savings and investment for employees of
the Medical Group.

         2. When did the plan go into effect?

                 The Cash or Deferred Profit Sharing Plan and Trust Agreement originally became
effective as of January 1, 1981 and has been amended. This summary plan description reflects all
plan amendments effective as of January 1, 2018.

         3. Who is eligible to participate?

                 Any employee of the Medical Group who already is a participant of the plan will
continue to participate in the amended plan. Any other or new employee of the Medical Group who
has completed two years of service with the Medical Group without a break in service will become
eligible to share in the Medical Group contributions to the plan. You will become eligible to share
in the Medical Group contributions on the date you complete the eligibility requirements.
Notwithstanding the above, an employee may begin to make 401(k) salary reduction contributions
immediately upon commencing employment with the Medical Group.

                 A "year of service" means all periods of service taken into account equaling twelve
months. Service counted in computing years of service need not be consecutive or continuous and all
fractional periods of service, unless otherwise excluded, will be aggregated on the basis that 30 days
of service constitute a month of service (in the case of fractional months of service) or 365 days of
service equal one year of service. Period of service refers to the time period between when an employee
commences and severs employment. An employee will receive credit for any period of severance
consisting of less than 12 consecutive months. However, if an employee incurs a break in service,
service accrued before such break shall not be taken into account in determining an employee's years
of service. A break in service occurs after a period of severance of at least twelve months. For example,
if you are hired on September 4, 2016, and remain employed until January 4, 2018, you will be credited
with one year and four months of service. If you then sever employment,

                                                        2

Active147385346, I
                                                                                Appendix C

but then are rehired on April 1, 2018, and continue to remain employed through December 1, 2018,
you will be credited with two years of service (September 4, 2016, through January 4, 2018, credits
you with one year and four months of service, and April 1, 2018, through December 1, 2018, credits
you with eight months of service without a break in service). Following your completion of two
years of service without a break in service, you will be eligible to share in Medical Group
contributions made to the Plan.

                 Your years of service with Colorado Permanente Medical Group or with any other
Permanente group of physicians that provides medical service to another region of the health
maintenance organization known as the Kaiser Foundation Health Plan, Inc. will count toward your
years of service for eligibility purposes under this plan. In addition, if you became employed by the
Medical Group before January 1, 2010, your years of service with Kaiser Foundation Health Plan of
Colorado will count toward your years of service for eligibility and vesting purposes under this plan.
Finally, effective April 2, 2012, your years of service with Kaiser Foundation Health Plan, Inc., any
Kaiser Foundation Hospitals, and any Permanente Medical Group associated with Kaiser Foundation
Health Plan, Inc. will count toward your years of service for eligibility and vesting purposes under this
plan.

         4. How do I become a participant?

                 The Committee will determine who is eligible to become a participant and will send
notice of plan participation to each eligible employee. At that time, you may elect to make salary
reduction contributions to the plan. In order to share in any Medical Group matching contributions,
you must elect to reduce your compensation for contribution to this plan (see question 7).

         5. How is the plan administered?

                 The plan is administered jointly by a Committee and a Plan Administrator appointed
by the Medical Group. The Committee assumes the major responsibilities for the day-to-day
operation and interpretation of the plan, and the Plan Administrator is responsible for the reporting
and disclosure requirements of federal and state law. The assets of the plan are administered and
invested by the Trustee, in accordance with your investment instructions.

         6. What is the year of the plan?

                 The fiscal year of the Cash or Deferred Profit Sharing Plan and Trust begins on
January 1 and ends on December 31. The records of the plan and trust are maintained on the
plan year.

         7. What contributions are made to this plan each year?

                                    YOUR ELECTION TO MAKE
                            SALARY REDUCTION CONTRIBUTIONS

                 You may elect to reduce your salary and have the salary reduction amount contributed
to the plan on your behalf. Your salary reduction contributions may not exceed the lesser of 100% of
your compensation (which remains after all payroll withholding and deductions) or $18,500 in 2018

                                                        3

Active/47385346.1
                                                                                Appendix C

(subject to possible cost of living increases after 2018 in $500 increments) (the "401(k) limit").
Contact the Plan Administrator for information and election forms to begin your salary
reduction contributions.

                 Salary reduction contributions always will be nonforfeitable (100% vested). Your
total contributions to the Plan may be limited under IRS rules. The total amount that the Company
contributes to the Plan plus the total amount of any participant contributions (including salary
reduction contributions) is limited to 100% of your compensation up to a maximum total
contribution of $55,000 (plus the catch-up amount if you make catch-up contributions) for 2018
(subject to possible cost of living increases after 2018).

                 You will be able to designate the tax treatment of your contribution either as a
traditional before-tax contribution or as a Roth after-tax contribution.

                 Traditional Before-Tax Contributions

                 If you elect to treat your contribution as a traditional before-tax contribution, your
salary reduction contribution to the Plan will not be subject to federal income tax in the year earned
but will be taxed when distributed to you from the Plan. Your salary reduction contribution will
remain subject to FICA (Social Security tax). Earnings on your salary reduction contribution also
will be taxed when they are distributed to you.

                 Roth After-Tax Contributions

                 If you elect to treat your contribution as a Roth after-tax contribution, your salary
reduction contribution to the Plan will remain subject to income tax (in addition to FICA taxes) in
the year earned. However, under current law, your Roth after-tax contribution will not be taxed when
distributed to you. In addition, if you maintain your Roth after-tax contributions in the Plan for at
least five years, then the earnings that accumulate on the Roth after-tax contributions also will not be
taxed when distributed to you, provided that such distribution occurs on account of your attainment
of age 59-1/2, your disability, or your death.

                 Whether you should elect to have your contributions to the Plan treated as traditional
before tax contributions or Roth after tax contributions is an important decision with a significant tax
impact. You should consult with your tax advisor regarding this decision.

                                    YOUR ELECTION TO MAKE
                                   CATCH-UP CONTRIBUTIONS

                 In addition, if you reach age 50 by the last day of the calendar year (December 31),
you may contribute an additional $6,000 as a salary reduction contribution to the Plan for the Plan
Year. This is called a "catch-up" contribution, and the catch-up contribution amount is $6,000 in 2018
(this amount may be subject to cost-of-living adjustments in subsequent years). No matching
contribution will be made to the Plan due to catch-up contributions. Your catch-up contributions will
be designated as Traditional before-tax contributions or Roth after-tax contributions in the same
proportion as your other 401(k) contributions.

                                                        4

Active/47385346.1
                                                                                Appendix C

                       MEDICAL GROUP MATCHING CONTRIBUTION

                 The Medical Group will make a matching contribution on behalf of each participant
who elects to make salary reduction contributions if the participant has completed the service
requirement for participation in Medical Group contributions (see question 3). No matching
contributions will be made based upon catch-up contributions. The matching contribution will be
determined by the Medical Group in its discretion, but it is the Medical Group's intention to make
these matching contributions in the highest amounts available while satisfying the limits on matching
contributions imposed under the Internal Revenue Code. Normally, the matching amount will equal
the deferred variable compensation divided by the 401(k) limit. Someone contributing $10,000 would
receive a match of $10,000. Therefore, those doctors who elect to contribute the full 401(k) limit (the
maximum allowed for 2018 is $18,500), if so determined by the Medical Group will have an amount
equal to their deferred variable compensation amount contributed to the plan as well. If another doctor
wants no match, he or she would elect no salary reductions, and, therefore, no match would be made
by the Medical Group. Doctors who do not want the full match would adjust their deferral election
accordingly. These matching contributions will be considered Medical Group contributions, will be
determined by the Medical Group, will not be taxable to you until you receive a distribution from the
plan, and will reduce your deferred variable compensation for the year if so determined by the Medical
Group. The total amount the Medical Group contributes on your behalf for any year as a matching
contribution may not exceed your deferred variable compensation for the year and will be determined
solely by the Medical Group.

                                                 EXAMPLES

                 The plan contribution provisions can be illustrated by the following examples.

                                                   Example 1

                 Doctors A, B, C, and D each are awarded deferred variable compensation of $18,500
for 2018. The Medical Group may announce a match of $1.00 for each dollar of salary or variable
compensation deferral reduction up to a maximum matching contribution of $18,500.

                 Doctor A. In order to receive a full match, Doctor A elects salary reductions
throughout the year of $18,500. This amount will be matched by the $18,500 deferred variable
compensation, which results in a total contribution of $37,000.

                 Doctor B. Doctor B wants to defer an amount equal to his or her deferred variable
compensation but no more. Doctor B elects a salary reduction, out of his or her deferred variable
compensation or regular compensation, of $9,250 which results in a matching contribution of $9,250
for a total contribution of $18,500.

                 Doctor C. Doctor C wants a total contribution of $5,000. He or she elects to
contribute $2,500 to the plan resulting in a matching contribution of $2,500, for a total
contribution of $5,000.

                                                        5

Active/47385346.I
                                                                                 Appendix C

                 Doctor D. Doctor D wants no match in this plan; therefore, Doctor D elects no
salary reduction either out of his or her variable compensation or from regular compensation.

                                                   Example 2

                 Doctors A, B, C, and D each are awarded deferred variable compensation of $11,100
for 2018. The Medical Group may announce a match of $0.60 for each $1.00 of salary reduction up to
a maximum matching contribution of $11,100. Assume each doctor wants to contribute as provided in
the first example.

                 Doctor A. Doctor A still will elect $18,500 in salary reductions for 2018. This
amount will be matched by the $11,100 equal to his or her deferred variable compensation and
a total $29,600 will be contributed on behalf of Doctor A.

                 Doctor B. Doctor B wants a contribution in an amount equal to his or her deferred
variable compensation, but not more. Doctor B will elect a salary reduction of $6,937.50 and it will
be matched by $4,162.50, for a total contribution of $11,100.

                 Doctor C. Doctor C wants a contribution of only $5,000 to the plan. Doctor C will
elect a salary reduction of $3,125, resulting in a match of $1,875, for a total contribution of $5,000.

                 Doctor D. Doctor D will elect no salary reduction.

                 YOUR NONDEDUCTIBLE VOLUNTARY CONTRIBUTIONS

                 You may want to make nondeductible voluntary contributions to the plan in addition
to, or instead of, the other contributions you may make to the plan. Your nondeductible voluntary
contributions will be taxed as "ordinary income" in the year in which you make the contribution;
however, the earnings on the contributions will not be taxed until they are distributed at some later
date. Therefore, you can accumulate some tax deferred income, and you will receive your
nondeductible voluntary contributions back tax-free at the time of distribution. All voluntary
contributions will be made in accordance with rules established by the Committee and always will be
nonforfeitable.

                                             COMPENSATION

                 Generally, your "compensation" for purposes of the Plan will include the total amount
paid to you for services rendered to the Company during a Plan Year reported as compensation on Form
W-2. The following types of compensation are excluded:

                     x distributions from the Company's non-qualified deferred compensation plans
                     x expense reimbursements -- accountable plan
                     x qualified moving expense reimbursements
                     x nontaxable fringe benefits
                     x worker's compensation
                     x nonqualified plan contributions excludable in the year of contribution

                      x statutory stock options includible in income in the year granted
                      x post-severance nonqualified deferred compensation and post-severance

                           --other payments
                      x amounts attributable to taxable fringe benefits, except for flex credits

                 The following types of compensation are included:

                      x any salary reduction contributions you have made to this plan, a cafeteria
                           plan, a SEPP plan, a 403(b) Plan, and any qualified transportation expense
                           plan maintained by the Company

                      x expense reimbursements -- nonaccountable plan
                      x fringe benefits to 2% shareholders of S-Corporations
                      x nonqualified moving expense reimbursements
                      x excess group term life insurance
                      x taxable medical or disability benefits
                      x differential wage payments
                      x medical loss ratio rebates attributable to salary reduction contributions

                           under a cafeteria plan
                      x severance payments paid within 2-1/2 months after your severance from

                           employment for trailing compensation and PTO
                      x salary continuation payments if you are disabled or for military service

                 This is only a general definition of the compensation that is included/excluded
for Plan purposes. Please see the Plan Administrator for additional details.

         8. What happens to contributions to this plan?

                 All contributions to the Plan are deposited with the Trustee. The duty of the Trustee is
to invest and reinvest the money deposited with it in accordance with your investment designations.
The Plan is intended to be an "ERISA Section 404(c) Plan." Under an ERISA ' 404(c) Plan, if
participants provide investment instructions for the investment of their accounts in compliance with
ERISA ' 404(c), the plan fiduciaries will not be liable for investment losses that are the direct result of
the participant's investment instructions.

                 Your investment choices, and the procedures for directing the investment of your
Account, are described in the investment materials available from the Committee. Information about
your investment alternatives, the investment objectives of each investment alternative, and the risk and
return characteristics of each investment alternative are available from the Committee.

         9. What happens to the earnings on contributions?

                 The earnings and losses on the investments that you select for your Account will
be credited directly to your Account.

                                                        7

Active/47385346.1
                                                                                Appendix C

         10. May I borrow money from my share in the plan?

                 The Committee may establish a uniform and nondiscriminatory policy for making
participant loans. Loans are available to all plan participants if the participant meets the credit-
worthiness and financial need requirements that would be considered in a normal commercial setting
by an entity in the business of making similar types of loans. Loans may not be taken from Roth after-
tax contributions and earnings thereon. A loan, when added to all other loans under the plan to any
individual participant may not exceed the lesser of: [a] $50,000, reduced by the excess of the highest
outstanding loan balance during the year before the loan date over the outstanding loan balance on the
loan date, or [b] the greater of one-half of the value of his vested Account balance or $10,000. The
Committee generally discourages loans because the deductibility of the interest often is precluded and
because of the legal pitfalls involved in plan loans. Most participants will have more flexibility if they
borrow elsewhere.

                 Loans from this plan are subject to several conditions that you must meet and to
which you must agree. These conditions and the procedures for applying for a loan are described
in the attached Participant Loan Procedures.

         11. May I withdraw money from my share in the plan while I remain employed
by the Company?

                 After you have completed two years of participation in the Plan, you may withdraw
any portion of your Account attributable to Medical Group contributions from the Plan. The Account
balance attributable to Medical Group contributions will not include any amount held in the trust
fund for less than two years and will not include any portion of your Account attributable to
contributions used to satisfy the Code Section 401(k) non-discrimination tests. The Plan
Administrator will provide you with information on the amount available for withdrawal, at your
request.

                 If you have attained age 59-1/2, you may withdraw any portion of your Account
balance attributable to Medical Group contributions, including earnings.

                 If you have attained age 59-1/2, you may withdraw any portion of your salary
reduction contributions to the Plan, including earnings, at any time. However, if you take an in-service
withdrawal from Roth after-tax contributions that have not been maintained in the Plan for at least
five years, you will be taxed on the in-service withdrawal of the earnings accumulated on such Roth
after-tax contributions.

                 You may request any of the withdrawals described above at any time by submitting a
written or electronic request for withdrawal to the financial institution where your Account balance is
invested, which, upon approval by the financial institution, will then distribute the amount you have
requested. If you make such a withdrawal, your Account will be credited with the earnings, losses,
and changes in fair market value as of the Valuation Date on which the withdrawal is processed by
the Plan.

                                                        8

Active/47385346.1
                                                                                Appendix C

                 In addition to age 59-1/2 withdrawals, if you have made salary reduction contributions
to the trust fund, including out of your deferred variable compensation, you may withdraw those
amounts, excluding earnings on those amounts after December 31, 1988, upon an immediate and
heavy financial need (Roth after-tax contributions and earnings thereon may not be taken as hardship
distributions). Financial needs that are considered immediate and heavy include: certain medical
expenses of you and your dependents; costs directly related to the purchase of your principal residence;
payment of tuition and related educational fees for the next twelve months of postsecondary education
for you and your dependents; the prevention of your eviction or the prevention of the foreclosure on
the mortgage of your principal residence; funeral expenses for your parent, spouse, child or other
dependent; and payment for expenses to repair damage to your principal residence (that would qualify
for a casualty loss deduction under the Internal Revenue Code), including damage due to fire, natural
disaster, or other similar unforeseeable event. Withdrawal of amounts on account of an immediate and
heavy financial need cannot exceed the amount necessary to meet the financial need and the amount
of the financial need cannot be reasonably available from other resources. Other resources that you
must exhaust before a hardship withdrawal will be made include loans from commercial sources and
from this Plan, insurance reimbursement, reasonable liquidation of your assets, and your cessation of
salary reduction contributions or deferred variable compensation deferrals. You will not be permitted
to make salary reductions or deferred variable compensation deferrals to the plan for six months after
you receive the withdrawn funds, and the withdrawn funds are not eligible for rollover.

                 Withdrawals of contributions made by the Medical Group or salary reduction
contributions prior to age 59-1/2 may be subject to a 10% penalty tax on "early distributions." The
10% penalty tax generally will not be imposed upon withdrawals made on account of the
participant's death, disability, attainment of age 55 and separation from service, payments over life
expectancy, rollovers to an IRA or another qualified plan, for certain medical expenses, and other
exceptions. Please see the Plan Administrator for additional information.

                 Generally, as described in Question 7, if you maintain your Roth after-tax
contributions in the Plan for at least five years, then the earnings that accumulate on the Roth
after-tax contributions also will not be taxed when you withdraw the amounts from the Plan.

                 You are permitted to rollover any amount, including amounts not otherwise eligible
for distribution under the Plan, to the designated Roth After-Tax Contribution Account under the
Plan. If you have questions regarding whether a distribution or in-service withdrawal of an amount
from your Account under the Plan is eligible to be rolled over to the Roth After-Tax Contribution
Account under the Plan, please see your Plan Administrator. If you roll over a payment to a
designated Roth account in the same plan, the amount of the payment rolled over (reduced by any
after-tax amounts directly rolled over) will be taxed and you must be prepared to pay that tax.
However, the 10% additional tax on early distributions will not apply (unless you take the amount
rolled over out of the designated Roth account within the 5-year period that begins on January 1 of
the year of the rollover).

                 You may withdraw all or any portion of your nondeductible voluntary
contributions or rollover contributions to the Plan at any time.

Active/47385346, 1
                                                                                Appendix C

                  Additional withdrawals are available if you are a reservist or national guardsman
and you are ordered or called to active duty. Please see the Plan Administrator for additional
information.

                  You should contact the Plan Administrator for further information on withdrawing
money from the Plan.

         12. What happens to my Account if I terminate employment?

                  Once you have become a participant in the plan, you always will be 100% vested
in your Account. This means that if you terminate employment for any reason, your total benefit
will be determined by the full value of your Account balance when it becomes distributable.

         13. When are benefits payable?

                  Your Account balance will be retained and kept invested in the trust fund until you
retire, become totally disabled, die, or otherwise terminate your employment with the Medical Group.
Distribution of your Account will be made in cash or, at your request, the distribution will be made
in-kind. Distribution of your Account will commence, with your consent, within an administratively
reasonable time after the date on which you retire, become totally disabled, die, or terminate your
employment or at any later date. If your Account balance does not exceed $1,000, (including any
rollovers you have made to this Plan), your Account balance will be distributed within a reasonable
time after the date on which termination of employment occurs, without the need for your consent.

                  Distributions must begin no later than the April 1 of the calendar year following
the later of (i) the calendar year in which you attain age 70-1/2 or (ii) the calendar year in which
you retire. However, if your are a 5% owner of the Company, distribution of your Account must
begin no later than the April 1 of the calendar year following the calendar year in which you attain
age 70-1/2.

                  a. What is my retirement date?

                  Your normal retirement date as a plan participant will be the day on which you
reach age 65.

                  b. What is "total disability"?

        Total disability means a disability that permanently renders a participant unable to perform
      satisfactorily, the usual duties of his employment with the Medical Group as determined by a
   physician selected by the Committee and that results in his termination of employment with the

                                                                                                   Medical Group.

                                                         10

Active/47385346.1
                                                                                Appendix C

   CONSEQUENCES OF FAILING TO DEFER RECEIPT OF YOUR DISTRIBUTION

                  If your vested benefit exceeds $1,000, you have the right to defer your distribution
until the later of Normal Retirement Age (Age 65) or age 62. You will be taxed on a payment from
the Plan if you do not roll it over. Distributions prior to age 59-1/2 may be subject to a 10% penalty
tax on "early distributions." The 10% penalty tax generally will not be imposed upon distributions
because of your death, disability, attainment of age 55 and separation from service, payments over
your life expectancy, rollovers to an IRA or another qualified plan, or distributions for certain
medical expenses.

                  Generally, your distribution will be subject to mandatory 20% income tax withholding
unless you elect a direct rollover distribution to an IRA or to the qualified plan of another employer.

                  You may elect to roll over your distribution to either an IRA (an individual retirement
account or individual retirement annuity) or an employer plan (a tax--qualified plan, section 403(b)
plan, or governmental section 457(b) plan) that will accept the rollover. The rules of the IRA or
employer plan that holds the rollover will determine your investment options, fees, and rights to
payment from the IRA or employer plan (for example, no spousal consent rules apply to IRAs and
IRAs may not provide loans).

                  If you do not elect a rollover to an IRA or employer plan, but instead elect to receive a
lump sum cash distribution, note that the income tax imposed [the withholding is at a flat 20%, not at
your current income tax rate] on such distribution will be assessed at your currently applicable income
tax rate. Not deferring receipt of your distribution until the later of Normal Retirement Age or Age 62
may result in the loss of future tax-favored treatment of any earnings on the amount of such distribution,
had such distribution instead remained in the Plan.

                  Note that some plan investment options in the Plan may not be generally available
on similar terms outside the Plan. Additionally, fees and expenses associated with investment options
available to you outside the Plan (including administrative or investment-related fees) may be
different from fees and expenses that apply to your Account in the Plan. For further information
regarding the fees and expenses that apply to your Account, contact the Plan Administrator.

         14. How will my benefits be computed?

                  The Committee and the Trustee determine the total value of the trust fund on each
business day that the stock market is open (the "Valuation Dates"). On each Valuation Date, the
Committee will compute the value of each participant's Account balance. If you become eligible to
receive a distribution, the distribution will be an amount which is equal to the value of your vested
Account. The Account value will be determined as of a Valuation Date which is after the date your
properly completed distribution forms are received and processed by the Committee. Your
distribution forms will be processed within an administratively reasonable period of time after the
forms are received by the Committee.

         15. How will I receive my benefits?

             Your Account balance will be distributed to you in a lump sum distribution.

                                                        11

Active/47385346.1
                                                                                Appendix C

          16. Can benefits be rolled over into an IRA or other qualified retirement plan?

                  Generally, distributions which are not directly transferred to an IRA or other qualified
retirement plan in a direct rollover distribution are subject to a mandatory 20% withholding for federal
income tax. Upon your entitlement to receive a distribution from the plan, the Plan Administrator will
provide you with a notice explaining the federal income tax withholding rules, the exceptions to the
withholding rules, and the requirements for a direct rollover of your distribution to an IRA or other
qualified retirement plan. The tax consequences of a retirement plan distribution can be complicated.
You should consult with a tax adviser because the Plan Administrator and other persons associated
with the Plan cannot provide personal tax advice to any Participant. You also may want to consult
IRS Publication 575, Pension and Annuity Income, which is available annually from the IRS free of
charge.

          17. What happens to my Account if I die?

                  If you die before distribution of your entire Account has been made, your Account
balance will be distributed to your surviving spouse, or if there is no surviving spouse or if your
spouse consents in writing, the balance will be distributed to the beneficiary or beneficiaries you
have designated within five years after your death.

          18. How do I designate a beneficiary?

                  If you are not married or if your spouse elects not to receive your Account in
accordance with procedures established by the Committee, your Account will be distributed to the
beneficiary or beneficiaries you have designated. To designate a beneficiary, you must complete a
Beneficiary Designation Form. It is important to keep a current beneficiary designation on file at all
times so that this important asset will be handled according to your wishes. The form may be changed
at any time. If you fail to designate a beneficiary or if the beneficiary or beneficiaries you have
designated die before you do, your Account balance will be paid in this order:

                  a. First to your spouse, and if he or she is not living;
                  b. To your descendants by right of representation, and if they are not living;
                  c. Then to the personal representative of your estate.

          19. What remedy do I have if my benefits under the plan are denied?

                  A claim for benefits may be filed with the Committee by you, by your duly authorized
representative, or by your beneficiary. The Committee will review your claim and will notify you as to
whether your claim has been granted or denied within 90 days after its receipt of the claim, unless
special circumstances require an extension of time for processing the claim. If an extension is required,
you will be notified in writing before expiration of the initial 90-day period. If your claim is denied,
you will receive a written notice explaining the denial in detail. You or your duly authorized
representative may file a written request with the Committee for review of the claim within 60 days
after you are notified of the denial. When you file a request for review, the Medical Group will appoint
a claims reviewer who will make and explain his decision on the claim to you within 60 days of receipt
of your request unless special circumstances require an extension of time

                                                       12

Active/47385346, I
                                                                                Appendix C

for processing, in which case a decision will be made not later than 120 days after receipt of
your request. If an extension is necessary, you will receive written notice of the extension prior
to the expiration of the 60-day period.

         20. What other rights do I have under the law?

                  As a participant in the Cash or Deferred Profit Sharing Plan and Trust Agreement, you
are entitled to certain rights and protections under the Employee Retirement Income Security Act of
1974. ERISA provides that all plan participants shall be entitled to:

                  a. Examine, without charge, at the Plan Administrator's office and at other
                           specified locations, such as worksites and union halls, all Plan documents
                           including insurance contracts, collective bargaining agreements, and a copy
                           of the latest annual report (Form 5500 Series) filed by the Plan with the U.S.
                           Department of Labor, and available at the Public Disclosure Room of the
                           Employee Benefits Security Administration.

                  b. Obtain, upon written request to the Plan Administrator, copies of documents
                           governing the Plan, including insurance contracts and collective bargaining
                           agreements, and a copy of the latest annual report (Form 5500 Series) and
                           updated summary plan description. The Administrator may make a
                           reasonable charge for the copies.

                  c. Receive a summary of the Plan's annual financial report. The Plan
                           Administrator is required by law to furnish each participant with a copy
                           of this summary financial report.

                  d. Obtain a statement telling you whether you have a right to receive a benefit at
                           normal retirement age (age 65) and if so, what your benefits would be at normal
                           retirement age if you stop working under the Plan now. If you do not have a
                           right to a benefit, the statement will tell you how many more years you have to
                           work to get a right to a benefit. This statement must be requested in writing and
                           is not required to be given more than once every twelve months. The Plan must
                           provide the statement free of charge.

                  In addition to creating rights for Plan participants, ERISA imposes duties upon the
people who are responsible for the operation of the employee benefit plan. The people who operate
your Plan, called "fiduciaries" of the Plan, have a duty to do so prudently and in the interest of you
and other Plan participants and beneficiaries. No one, including your employer, your union, or any
other person, may fire you or otherwise discriminate against you in any way to prevent you from
obtaining a benefit or exercising your rights under ERISA.

                  If your claim for a benefit is denied or ignored, in whole or in part, you have a right to
know why this was done, to obtain copies of documents relating to the decision without charge, and to
appeal any denial, all within certain time schedules. Under ERISA, there are steps you can take to enforce
the above rights. For instance, if you request a copy of Plan documents or the latest annual

                                                       13

Active/47385346,1
                                                                                Appendix C

report from the Plan and do not receive them within 30 days, you may file suit in a federal court. In
such a case, the court may require the Plan Administrator to provide the materials and pay you up to
$110 a day until you receive the materials, unless the materials were not sent because of reasons beyond
the control of the Administrator. If you have a claim for benefits which is denied or ignored, in whole
or in part, you may file suit in a state or federal court. In addition, if you disagree with the Plan's decision
or lack thereof concerning the qualified status of a domestic relations order, you may file a suit in
federal court.

                 If it should happen that Plan fiduciaries misuse the Plan's money, or if you are
discriminated against for asserting your rights, you may seek assistance from the U.S. Department of
Labor, or you may file suit in a federal court. The court will decide who should pay court costs and
legal fees. If you are successful, the court may order the person you have sued to pay these costs and
fees. If you lose, the court may order you to pay these court costs and fees, for example, if it finds your
claim is frivolous.

                 If you have any questions about the Plan, you should contact the Plan Administrator
or Plan Committee at the addresses on the last page of this summary. If you have any questions about
this summary or about your rights under ERISA, or if you need assistance in obtaining documents
from the Plan Administrator, you should contact the nearest office of the Employee Benefits Security
Administration, U.S. Department of Labor, listed in your telephone directory or the Division of
Technical Assistance and Inquiries, Employee Benefits Security Administration, U.S. Department of
Labor, 200 Constitution Avenue N.W., Washington, D.C. 20210. You also may obtain certain
publications about your rights and responsibilities under ERISA by calling the publications hotline of
the Employee Benefits Security Administration.

        21. What other provisions are important to me?

                  a. You cannot assign or encumber any of the benefits which you may expect to
                          receive under the plan, nor can any of your share in Medical Group
                          contributions be made subject to the claim of any creditor. However, under a
                          qualified domestic relations order, all or a portion of the benefits payable to
                          a participant may be assigned to an alternate payee under procedures
                          established by the Committee. Participants and beneficiaries can obtain,
                          without charge, a copy of the qualified domestic relations order procedures
                          from the Plan Administrator. A domestic relations order is any judgment,
                          decree, or order (including approval of property settlement agreement) that
                          relates to the provision of child support, alimony payments, or marital
                          property rights to a spouse, former spouse, child, or other dependent of a
                          participant, and is made pursuant to a state domestic relations law.

                  b. The Cash or Deferred Profit Sharing Plan and Trust Agreement has been
                          designed to allow you, in the discretion of the Committee, to rollover
                          distributions from another qualified retirement plan to this plan and to rollover
                          your share in this plan to another qualified plan. Because the rules concerning
                          such rollovers are extremely complex, you must consult directly with the
                          Committee if you desire to make a rollover contribution to this plan

                                                       14

Active/47385346,1
                                                                                Appendix C

                           or any other plan. A written explanation of the rollover and direct
                           transfer rules will be provided under the plan each time an eligible
                           rollover distribution is made.

                  c. Participation in the plan does not confer upon you any right of continued
                           employment.

                  d. The Medical Group expects to continue this plan indefinitely. However, to
                           protect the Medical Group against unforeseen conditions, it reserves the right
                           to reduce or temporarily suspend contributions or to amend or terminate the
                           plan in whole or in part at any time. If the plan is terminated, the balance of
                           your Account attributable to Medical Group contributions will remain 100%
                           vested (nonforfeitable).

                  e. Benefits under this plan are not insured by the Pension Benefit Guaranty
                           Corporation because the plan is an individual account plan not covered by the
                           statutory insurance provisions.

                           The Cash or Deferred Profit Sharing Plan and Trust Agreement has very
                           substantial tax advantages to you as a participant. Even though your share in
                           the Medical Group's contribution may be partially or fully vested, you pay no
                           income tax on the contribution or on your traditional before-tax contributions
                           until your Account actually is distributed to you. The tax impact of your Roth
                           after-tax contributions is described in Question 7. All income and profits on
                           investments in the trust fund usually are tax exempt to the trust. Thus, the plan
                           provides tax deferment to the participant on the Medical Group's contributions
                           and on the income and profits earned by Medical Group and participant
                           contributions.

                g. If you are absent from work because of active military duty, you may have
                           certain rights under the Plan under the Uniformed Services Employment and
                           Reemployment Rights Act (USERRA) upon your return to employment,
                           including the right to make up contributions for the period of your military
                           service. Please contact the Plan Administrator for more information about
                           these rights.

                      COLORADO PERMANENTE MEDICAL GROUP, P.C.
                 CASH OR DEFERRED PROFIT SHARING PLAN AND TRUST

                                 PARTICIPANT LOAN PROCEDURES

                   Pursuant to Section 7.5 of the Colorado Permanente Medical Group, P.C. Cash or
Deferred Profit Sharing Plan and Trust, loans to participants that are made on or after January 1,
2007, must comply with the following procedures:

          1. The Vanguard Group shall be authorized to administer the loan program.

          2. To apply for a loan, the participant must contact the Loan Administrator with the
following information concerning the loan:

                   a. Amount of loan requested
                   b. Purpose of the loan
                   c. Requested term of the loan: The repayment period shall not exceed five years,

                            unless the loan is for the acquisition of the principal residence of the participant,
                            in which case the term may be as long as ten years, as determined by the Plan
                            Administrator. Loans may be prepaid in full at any time.

          3. The Loan Administrator will approve a plan loan if the following items are
         satisfied:

                   a. The amount requested must be within the limits prescribed by the Internal
                            Revenue Code. Generally, the limit is the lesser of 1) $50,000 or 2) the
                            greater of 1/2 the participant's account or $10,000. A participant cannot
                            request a loan from his or her designated Roth after-tax contribution account
                            or the earnings thereon.

                   b. Adequate security is pledged for the loan. This means that the loan is secured
                            by something in addition to a promise to pay, that is so pledged to the plan that
                            it may be sold, foreclosed upon, or otherwise disposed of upon a default of
                            repayment of the loan. The participant may secure the loan with up to 50% of
                            his account balance. Although a participant cannot take a loan distribution
                            from his or her designated Roth after-tax contribution account and earnings
                            thereon, such designated Roth amounts may be used for purposes of providing
                            adequate security for a loan.

          4. Limitations on types and amounts of loans:

                   a. Minimum loan permitted - None
                   b. Maximum loan permitted - Maximum permitted by law
                   c. No more than two loans may be outstanding at any time.

          5. The interest rate for the loan shall be 1.5% over the Prime rate charged by The
Vanguard Group. The term Prime rate will be the Prime rate in effect as first published by The Wall
Street Journal in its Money Rates column each Federal Reserve Board meeting. Notwithstanding

                                                           i

Active/47385346.1
                                                                               Appendix C

anything to the contrary herein, the rate of interest shall not exceed, or shall be reduced to, six
percent (6%) per year during any part of a period of military service for persons covered by the
Soldiers' and Sailors' Civil Relief Act of 1940, as amended.

         6. If any loan payment is not made by the end of the calendar quarter following the
calendar quarter in which the loan payment was due, the entire loan balance will be considered in
default, as required under IRS rules, and will be taxable to the participant. Upon the default of any
loan, the Loan Administrator may take such steps as he may be entitled under law to ensure
repayment of the loan.

         7. If a participant terminates employment with the Company and the participant loan has
not been fully repaid within ninety (90) days following such termination of employment, the loan will
be considered in default, and the unpaid loan balance and any interest owed on the loan will be taxable
to the participant and will be deducted from the amount distributed to the terminated participant, or to
the beneficiary of a deceased participant, in full satisfaction of the outstanding loan.

         8. Unless elected in a. or b. below, the Plan Administrator will not suspend loan
repayments during leaves of absence.

                           a. Loan repayments shall be suspended during a duly authorized leave of
                           absence without pay, or a leave of absence at a rate of pay (after income and
                           employment tax withholding) that is less than the amount of the installment
                           payments required under the terms of the loan, provided the leave does not
                           extend beyond one year and does not extend beyond the period for repayment
                           required by Code Section 72(p)(2)(B).

                           b. Loan repayments shall be suspended during a leave of absence due
                           to military service within the meaning of Code Section 414(u)(4) until the
                           participant's completion of military service or until the participant's fifth
                           anniversary of commencement of military service, if earlier.

When payments resume following a suspension in connection with a leave of absence authorized
in a. or b. above, if applicable, the participant shall select one of the following methods to repay
the loan, plus accumulated interest, as elected below (if no option is elected, item 1. shall be deemed
to have been elected):

                                    1. The participant may increase the amount of the required
                                    installments to an amount sufficient to amortize the remaining
                                    balance of the loan, plus accrual interest, over the remaining term of
                                    the loan.

                                    2. The participant shall pay a balloon payment of the remaining
                                    unpaid principal and interest, at the conclusion of the term of the loan
                                    as determined by the promissory note.

                                    3. The participant may extend the maturity of the loan and
                                    reamortized the payments over the remaining term of the loan. In no

                                                          ii

Active/47385346.1
                                                                                Appendix C

                                     event shall the amount of the adjusted installment payment be less
                                     than the amount of the installment payment provided under the
                                     promissory note. In the case of a suspension permitted under a., the
                                     revised term of the loan shall not exceed the maximum term
                                     permitted under Section 2.c. In the case of a suspension permitted
                                     under b., the loan shall not exceed the maximum term permitted
                                     under Section 2.c, plus the period of military service.
         9. Loans may be taken from the following accounts in the following order:
                   a. Rollovers (excluding any Roth characterized amounts and earnings thereon)
                   b. Company discretionary contributions
                   c. Company matching contributions
                   d. Participant elective deferrals (excluding Roth after-tax contributions and
                            earnings thereon)
                        Loans are not available from individual brokerage accounts
                   The Plan Committee of the Colorado Permanente Medical Group, P.C. Cash or
Deferred Profit Sharing Plan and Trust approved and adopted these loan procedures as part of the
Plan and Trust.
